The dwarves were skeptical. They had forged weapons for kings and heroes. They had never forged a weapon for the son of a god.


"We will need something from you," the dwarf king said. "Something of equal value."


Thors reached into his chest. He pulled out a spark of his own lightning. It crackled in his palm, brighter than the forge fires. He placed it on the anvil.


The dwarves stared.


"That is not possible," the dwarf king said.


"I am not possible," Thors said.


The dwarves forged the hammer for seven days and seven nights. They named it Mjölnir. It was not a hammer of metal. It was a hammer of crystallized lightning, bound in iron, wrapped in leather from a sea serpent Thors had killed on the voyage south.


It was heavier than any mortal could lift. Thors lifted it with one hand.


When he swung Mjölnir, thunder boomed across the mountains. When he struck the ground, lightning split the earth. When he threw it, it always returned to his hand.


The dwarves asked for nothing else. The spark was enough.


---


## PART SEVEN: THE WORLD SERPENT


Deep in the Sapphire Expanse, in the darkest trenches where the sun never reached, Abyssa had been working. She had taken the corpse of a leviathan, a creature so old that its bones had turned to stone, and she had breathed madness into it. She had fed it the dreams of drowned sailors and the screams of the damned. She had grown it for centuries.


She called it Jörmungandr, the World Serpent.


It was not a serpent in the way mortals understood serpents. It was a wound in the ocean, a darkness that moved, a hunger that consumed. Its body was miles long. Its scales were like obsidian. Its eyes were like black suns. Where it swam, the water turned to poison. Where it surfaced, the sky turned to ash.


Abyssa released it in the year 490 AW.


The World Serpent rose from the deep off the coast of Nordvorn, not far from the fjords where Thors had been born. It destroyed three fishing villages in a single day. It swallowed ships whole. It breathed a fog that drove sailors mad.


The Skaldians fought. They could not stop it. The Vallian legions sent ships. The Serpent crushed them. The Qashari mages tried to banish it. The Serpent ignored them.


The Serpent coiled around the islands off the northern coast. It squeezed. The islands cracked. The people fled inland. Thousands died.


Abyssa watched from the depths. She was smiling.


---


## PART EIGHT: THE CALL


Thors heard the news in the highlands. He was three hundred years old. His mother Helga had been dead for two centuries. His wife Astrid had been dead for a century. His children were old, their children were old, their children's children were old. He had watched them all grow, flourish, and fade.


He was tired. He was lonely. He was ready.


He stood on the cliffs of his homeland, looking north toward the sea where the Serpent hunted. Mjölnir was in his hand. The sky was clear. The sea was calm.


"The World Serpent," he said. "Abyssa's monster."


He did not pray to Malakor. He did not need to.


"I am going," he said. "I am not coming back."


The wind picked up. The sky darkened. Thunder rumbled in the distance.


Malakor appeared beside him. The god of war stood on the cliffs, his eyes burning like forges.


"You know what this means," Malakor said.


"I know."


"You will die."


"I know."


"Your death will be felt across the world. The storms will rage for seven days. Every living thing will know that a great warrior has fallen."


Thors looked at his father. He did not smile. He did not frown.


"Let them know," he said.


Malakor nodded. He placed his hand on Thors's shoulder. It was the first time he had ever touched his son.


"Fight well," the god said.


"I always do."


Thors walked into the sea. He walked on the surface, lightning crackling around his feet, Mjölnir glowing in his hand.


The World Serpent sensed him. It turned from the islands. It swam toward him.


The battle began.


---


## PART NINE: THE SEVEN DAYS OF STORMS


The battle lasted for seven days and seven nights. It took place in the cold waters off the coast of Nordvorn, where the fjords met the open sea.


**On the first day,** the sky turned black. Lightning struck the sea a thousand times. The waves rose higher than the cliffs. The wind screamed like the damned. Across Terra, farmers looked up at the dark sky and wondered what had angered the gods.


**On the second day,** the storms spread south. Vallia was lashed by rain and hail. The streets of Aurelia flooded. The Tiber River rose over its banks. The people took shelter in their homes and prayed.


Thors threw Mjölnir. It struck the Serpent's eye. The Serpent screamed. The water turned to steam. Thors caught Mjölnir as it returned.


**On the third day,** Solarem was hit by sandstorms so fierce that the sun was blotted out. The Qashari mages tried to calm the winds. They could not. The storms were not natural. They were the death throes of a world.


Thors climbed the Serpent's body. His hands gripped its obsidian scales. Lightning coursed through him, through the Serpent, through the sea. The water boiled. The sky caught fire.


**On the fourth day,** Orentis was buried in fog so thick that people could not see their own hands. The Jin retreated into their hidden valleys and waited. They did not know what was happening. They only knew that something terrible was coming.


Thors reached the Serpent's neck. He raised Mjölnir. He brought it down. The hammer struck the Serpent's spine. The Serpent convulsed. Black blood poured into the sea.


**On the fifth day,** the Broken Isles were battered by waves that destroyed every dock and harbor. The Oru dragged their ships inland and prayed to Discordia. The pirate queen Adedoyin knelt on the shore and watched the sky. "Someone is dying," she said. "Someone great."


Thors was wounded. His arm was broken. His ribs were cracked. His skin was burned black. He did not stop.


**On the sixth day,** even the Elves felt the storms. The mountains of Sunspire were lashed by lightning. The Elthari watched from their spires. They said nothing. They knew.


Thors reached the Serpent's head. He raised Mjölnir one last time.


**On the seventh day,** the storms stopped. The sky cleared. The sun broke through. The world was silent.


Thors brought Mjölnir down on the Serpent's skull. The lightning that had been building inside him for three centuries exploded outward.


The sea rose in a wave that crashed against the cliffs of Nordvorn. The thunder was so loud that every living thing on Terra heard it.


When the light faded, the Serpent was dead. Its body sank into the deep.


Thors floated on the surface, alone, broken, dying. His body was burned beyond recognition. His eyes were still open. His hand still clutched Mjölnir.


He looked up at the clear sky. The sun was warm on his face.


He smiled.


He died.


---


## PART TEN: THE AFTERMATH


The skalds sang of the battle for generations. They called it the Battle of the Endless Storm. They said the whole world had wept for seven days. They said the sea had never been so wild. They said the sky had never been so dark.


They said Thors had saved the world.


They were right.


The World Serpent's body sank into the trench off the coast of Nordvorn. The poison faded. The sea healed. The islands that had been crushed were scarred but alive.


The Skaldians returned to their villages. They rebuilt. They never forgot.


The Vallians raised a statue of Thors on the coast of Silverport, facing north toward the battle site. They did not know him. They did not worship his god. But they honored him anyway.


The Skaldians built a great pyre on the cliffs where Thors had stood. They burned no body. There was no body. They burned his memory instead. The fire burned for seven days.


The skalds sang new songs. They sang of the Giant-Killer. The Storm-Born. The Thunder of the Fjords. The World Serpent's Bane.


They sang of a man who died so that others could live.


---


## PART ELEVEN: THE AFTERLIFE


Thors woke in a field of ash and lightning.


The sky was red. The ground was black. The air smelled of ozone and iron. In the distance, mountains of obsidian rose against a horizon of fire.


He was not in the Aurealis. He was not in the Great Foundation. He was not in the Twilight Labyrinth. He was not in Hell.


He was in Malakor's realm.


The god of war sat on a throne of fused iron and obsidian, surrounded by the skulls of worthy enemies. He was not smiling. He was not frowning. He was watching.


"You came," Malakor said.


"You knew I would."


"I hoped."


Thors looked at his hands. They were whole again. His skin was unburned. His eyes still glowed gold. Mjölnir was in his hand.


"What now?" Thors asked.


Malakor stood. He picked up his axe. It was massive, jagged, scarred from a thousand battles.


"Now we fight," Malakor said.


Thors smiled. It was the first time he had smiled since his mother died.


"Every day?"


"Every day."


"Until when?"


"Until the end of everything."


Thors raised Mjölnir. Lightning crackled across the sky.


"That sounds like forever."


"It is."


"Good."


They fought. Not as father and son. As warriors. As equals.


The battle lasted for a day. Then another. Then another. There was no end. There was no need for an end.


Thors fought beside his father. He fought against his father. He fought for the joy of fighting. He fought for the first time in centuries without the weight of mortality pressing on his chest.


He was not a hero here. He was not a legend. He was a warrior. That was enough.


Astrid was not here. His children were not here. His mother was not here. They were in the Great Foundation, at peace, resting.


Thors did not want peace. He wanted battle. He wanted the crash of steel, the boom of thunder, the crack of lightning.


He wanted his father.


Malakor did not speak of love. He did not speak of pride. He fought. That was his language. Thors understood.


They fought side by side.


The skalds sing of Thors as a hero. They sing of his sacrifice. They sing of the World Serpent's death. They sing of the seven days of storms that shook the world.


They do not sing of what came after. They do not know.


But Thors knows. Thors is there, in the red sky, on the black earth, fighting.


He is not lonely anymore.


---


# THE CULT OF THORS


## How the Skaldians Honor the Storm-Born


---


## The Hero of the Fjords


In every longhouse across Nordvorn, from the frozen shores of the north to the green lowlands of the south, there is a place for Thors. His name is spoken alongside the gods. His deeds are sung by every skald. His hammer, Mjölnir, is carved into doorposts, painted onto shields, and tattooed onto the arms of warriors.


The Skaldians do not worship Thors as a god. He was not a god. He was a demigod. He was mortal. He bled. He died. He saved them.


They revere him. They pray to him. They ask for his strength, his courage, his lightning.


*"Thors, who fought the World Serpent. Thors, who died so that we might live. Thors, who now fights beside his father in the red sky. Hear us."*


---


## Prayers to Thors


**Before Battle**


Skaldian warriors whisper a prayer to Thors. They do not shout it. The old ways say that Thors heard enough thunder in his life. He prefers silence now.


*"Thors, Storm-Born, lend me your strength. Let my arm be as unyielding as yours. Let my heart be as fierce as yours. Let my death, if it comes, be as worthy as yours."*


**Before a Sea Voyage**


Sailors pray to Thors for calm waters. The irony is not lost on them. The man who caused the Seven Days of Storms is now asked for gentle seas.


*"Thors, who walked on the waves, who fought the Serpent in the deep, who calmed the storms with his passing. Watch over us. Guide us home."*


**Before the Birth of a Child**


Mothers pray to Thors for protection.


*"Thors, who was born in a blizzard, who came into the world with lightning in his fists. Protect my child. Give them your strength. Spare them your fate."*


---


## Offerings


Skaldians leave offerings at the cliffs where Thors walked into the sea. They leave iron, for his hammer. They leave mead, for his thirst. They leave weapons, for his battles.


They do not leave bodies. Thors had enough of death.


The offerings are taken by the sea. The waves carry them away. The Skaldians believe that Thors receives them in Malakor's realm, where he fights forever.


---


## Festivals


The Feast of the Storm-Born is held every year on the anniversary of the Serpent's death. It lasts for seven days, one for each day of the great storm.


- **On the first day,** the Skaldians fast. They remember the darkness. They remember the fear.
- **On the second day,** they light bonfires along the coast. They pretend the fires are lightning.
- **On the third day,** they tell stories of Thors. Every clan has its own version. They argue about the details. They do not fight. Thors would not want them to fight over him.
- **On the fourth day,** they sail out to the battle site. They throw offerings into the water. They sing the songs of the Serpent's death.
- **On the fifth day,** they feast. They eat and drink until dawn. They toast to Thors. They toast to Malakor. They toast to the fallen.
- **On the sixth day,** they hold tournaments. Sword fights. Axe throws. Wrestling matches. The winners are called Thors-Kin for a year.
- **On the seventh day,** they are silent. They stand on the cliffs and watch the sea. They remember the day the storms stopped. They remember the day the sun broke through.


They remember that Thors died so that they could live.


---


## The Hammer Pendant


Nearly every Skaldian wears a hammer pendant. Mjölnir. Carved from iron, from bone, from driftwood. It is not a symbol of faith in a god. It is a symbol of faith in a hero.


They touch the pendant before battle. They kiss it before bed. They hold it when they are afraid.


*"Thors, be with me."*


---


## The Skalds' Songs


The skalds have composed hundreds of songs about Thors. The most famous is called *The Seven Days*. It begins:


*"On the first day, the sky went black.*
*The Serpent rose from the sea.*
*On the second day, the waves rose high.*
*The Serpent came for thee.*
*On the third day, the lightning struck.*
*The Serpent screamed in pain.*
*On the fourth day, the thunder roared.*
*The Serpent bled in vain.*
*On the fifth day, the winds did howl.*
*The Serpent coiled to strike.*
*On the sixth day, the sea ran red.*
*The Serpent met its night.*
*On the seventh day, the storms did cease.*
*The sun broke through the grey.*
*And Thors the Storm-Born went to rest.*
*The world was saved that day."*


Every Skaldian child knows this song. They learn it before they learn to read. They sing it at festivals. They whisper it at funerals.


---


## The Statues


Statues of Thors stand on every coast of Nordvorn. He is depicted with Mjölnir raised, his face turned toward the sea. His eyes are carved from amber. They catch the light. They seem to watch.


The oldest statue stands on the cliffs where he walked into the water. It has been there for over four thousand years. The sea has worn it smooth. The face is barely recognizable. The Skaldians do not care. They know who it is.


They leave offerings at its feet. Iron. Mead. Weapons. Flowers.


They touch its base before they sail.


*"Thors, watch over us."*


---


## The Children's Rhyme


Skaldian mothers tell their children a rhyme before bed:


*"Thors is watching from the sky.*
*Thors has lightning in his eye.*
*If you are brave, if you are true,*
*Thors will send his strength to you.*
*If you lie, if you are weak,*
*Thors will make the thunder speak."*


The children do not fear Thors. They love him. He is their hero. Their protector. The man who died so that they could live.


---


## The Warriors' Oath


Before a great battle, the warriors of the Fjord Clans swear an oath on Mjölnir. They hold the hammer pendant in their fists. They speak together:


*"I swear by Thors who fought the Serpent.*
*I swear by Malakor who gave him strength.*
*I swear by my ancestors who watched.*
*I will not flee. I will not yield. I will not break.*
*If I fall, let me fall forward.*
*If I die, let me die fighting.*
*Thors, Storm-Born, witness me."*


They believe that Thors hears them. They believe that he nods from the red sky, where he fights beside his father.


---


**END OF THORS STORM-BORN**


---




THE CHRONICLES OF VALLIA: THE EPIC OF ALEXANDER THE GREAT
Official Imperial Historiography — Formatted for Document Archive and Educational Registry
SECTION I: BIRTH, ANCESTRY, AND THE SEEDS OF AMBITION (105 AW – 120 AW)
The Cradle of Destiny
In 105 AW, Alexander was born within the walled city-state of Lysandria, a rising power situated in the fertile, river-fed plains of central Aurelia. He was born into a household of conflicting philosophies and legendary expectations:
* The Father: Nicolaus, the reigning Archon of Lysandria. He was a pragmatic, deeply cautious statesman who survived by balancing regional politics. He viewed survival, structural stability, and defensive preservation as far superior to the reckless pursuit of martial glory.
* The Mother: Hera, a high-ranking priestess of Astraea (The Star-Navigator), the goddess of cosmic intellect, the deep seas, and calculated travel. Hera was fiercely ambitious, instilling in her son the unshakeable belief that his bloodline was divinely ordained for global hegemony.
      [ NICOLAUS OF LYSANDRIA ]               [ HERA OF ASTRAEA ]
       (Pragmatism & Preservation)           (Divine Ambition & Intellect)
                    ▲                                      ▲
                    +------------------+-------------------+
                                       |
                           [ ALEXANDER THE VALLIAN ]
                       "Destined to rewrite the map."


The Shadow of the First Emperor
Throughout his youth, Alexander was raised on his mother's vivid accounts of Aurelian, the legendary first demigod, first emperor, and the greatest High Elf to ever walk the earth.
* The Blueprint of Conquest: Aurelian had successfully bound the warring elven tribes, broken the primordial wilderness, and engineered a system-spanning empire that stood unchallenged for millennia.
* The Codex Under the Pillow: Alexander slept every night with a stolen translation of the Aurelian Codex beneath his pillow. He memorized its tactical formations, logistical breakdowns, and philosophical treatises on sovereign power.
* The Laughter of the High Elves: When the elven emissaries and lords trading in Lysandria overheard the young human child openly declaring that he would one day match or surpass Aurelian's global conquests, they laughed openly at him. They viewed humans as short-lived, structurally inferior chaff. Alexander recorded their faces, their names, and their laughter. He never forgot.
SECTION II: THE ASSASSINATION AND THE ASCENSION (120 AW)
The Dorian Conspiracies
In 120 AW, the delicate geopolitical balance of central Aurelia shattered. Fearing the growing defensive networks and diplomatic influence of Nicolaus, the rival southern city-state of Dorian struck.
* The Plot: Orchestrated under the secret direction of Dorian’s Archon and heavily subsidized by foreign Elven agents seeking to keep the human city-states fragmented, an elite assassination squad infiltrated the Lysandrian palace.
* The Loss: Nicolaus was murdered in his solar. Though Alexander was devastated by the loss of a father who had meticulously trained him in swordplay, troop command, and domestic governance, he had no window to grieve.
The Eighteen-Year-Old Archon
With the state on the precipice of a cascading panic, Hera bypassed traditional mourning protocols. She immediately convened the Lysandrian City Council, delivering a blistering, calculated speech. She argued that while Alexander was only 18 years old, his unmatched martial training, theoretical mastery of the Aurelian Codex, and untamed ambition made him the sole entity capable of averting total annexation. Driven by her fervor and the imminent threat of Dorian's legions, the council voted unanimously. Alexander ascended as the youngest Archon in Lysandrian history.
SECTION III: THE UNIFICATION AND THE FOUR STRATEGIC GENERALS (121 AW – 126 AW)
Alexander immediately revolutionized the Lysandrian military. He discarded static defensive doctrines, implemented relentless physical conditioning regimens based on high-endurance tracking, and fundamentally altered troop morale by leading exclusively from the front vanguard. He ate standard field rations, slept on uninsulated soil alongside his recruits, and bled in the opening shock lines.
As he systematically marched across the central plains, conquering or absorbing neighboring city-states, his doctrine of unconditional battlefield dominance paired with magnanimous post-victory mercy turned historical rivals into fanatical loyalists. During this rapid consolidation, he bound his four legendary grand generals to his banner:
1. Julius of Dorian (The Mind of the Campaign) — Bound in 122 AW
* The Origin: The biological son of the Dorian Archon—the very man who had explicitly authorized the assassination of Alexander's father.
* The Subversion: When Alexander’s vanguard encircled the wealthy southern citadel of Dorian, Julius realized a protracted siege would mean the total annihilation of his people. Under a midnight flag of truce, Julius slipped into Alexander’s command tent. He offered an icy, pragmatic transaction: he would manually open the inner gates of Dorian from within, provided Alexander guaranteed his father's physical life and granted Julius a seat on his supreme war council.
* The Role: Alexander accepted. Dorian fell without the loss of a single civilian life. Julius proved to be a scheming, brilliant, hyper-calculating master of statecraft and grand strategy, consistently operating three moves ahead of the empire's enemies.
2. Honorius of Aureliopolis (The Iron Veteran) — Bound in 123 AW
* The Origin: A grizzled, heavily scarred commander and the Archon of Aureliopolis, a hardline warrior-citadel perched in the eastern hills that had resisted elven border incursions for generations.
* The Tragedy: Unlike Dorian, Aureliopolis refused to surrender. A catastrophic, bloody battle ensued outside the city walls. During the height of the chaotic infantry clash, Honorius’s son—the commander of the city's elite royal guard—was cut down by Alexander’s charging shock units.
* The Kneeling Conqueror: Following the breaking of the city, Alexander did not execute the leadership or sack the temples. He entered the grand forum, walked directly to the weeping, broken Honorius, and knelt completely before the old man. Alexander returned his son’s ancestral sword hilt-first, declaring: "Your son died with absolute honor. He fought like a titan. I do not come to enslave his father." Overwhelmed by this supreme displays of chivalric virtue, Honorius swore a binding blood oath to Alexander upon his son’s blade, becoming the senior commander of the imperial infantry and the sovereign royal guard.
3. Constantine of Thalassokratia (The Golden Merchant) — Bound in 124 AW
* The Origin: The sovereign ruler of Thalassokratia, the ultra-wealthy mercantile port city dominating the silver coast.
* The Transaction: Constantine possessed zero romantic interest in military glory or bleeding in the mud, but he possessed an exceptional eye for trade macroeconomics. As Alexander’s massive terrestrial war machine approached the coast, Constantine bypassed traditional deployment, sending a formal diplomatic envoy with a ready-made contract. He offered his entire sovereign fleet, unhindered port infrastructure, and total capitulation without a single arrow fired, in exchange for guaranteed tariff-free access to every domestic market within Alexander's expanding realm, alongside imperial naval protection for his merchant fleets.
* The Role: Alexander signed the decree. Constantine instantly stabilized the young empire’s economy, transforming into the Master of Logistics, managing the massive supply lines, grain reserves, and gold operations required to sustain a continental war.
4. Augustus of Kyropolis (The Shield of the Frontier) — Bound in 125 AW
* The Origin: The Archon of Kyropolis, an isolated, heavily exposed frontier settlement directly bordering the hostile ancestral deepwoods and elven holdings.
* The Rescue: Before Alexander’s army could even issue a standard diplomatic summons to Kyropolis, a massive, predatory fleet of Oru Pirates made landfall. The raiders incinerated the harbor warehouses, massacred local garrisons, and took thousands of citizens hostage.
* The Divergent March: Rather than utilizing the distraction to annex the weakened city, Alexander immediately turned his entire army eastward on a forced march to save it. He personally led a devastating cavalry charge that smashed the Oru lines, drove the survivors back into the deep ocean, and successfully recovered every hostage.
* The Oath: Augustus, humbled by a conqueror who chose protection over opportunistic subjugation, knelt in the ashes of his city and pledged his absolute life to the crown. He became the unbreakable shield of the frontier, permanently locking down the empire's borders.
SECTION IV: THE BIRTH OF THE VALLIANS (126 AW)
By 126 AW, the final independent city-state of the central plains had formally integrated. For the first time in documented history, the human populations of central Aurelia were unified under a single centralized authority, possessing an army massive enough to directly challenge the hegemony of the immortal Elves.
The Hill of Proclamation
To strip away the lingering regional tribalism of the old city-states, Alexander gathered his entire combined host—hundreds of thousands of soldiers—upon a sweeping hill overlooking the vast, rolling river valleys of their birthplace. He delivered the foundational decree of the empire:
"We are no longer Lysandrians, Dorians, or citizens of the coast. We are no longer fragmented city-states destined to be the sport of immortal lords. We are one blood. We are the masters of these valleys, and we will be the masters of this earth. From this day forward, you are called Vallians—born of these valleys, forged in this soil, and eternally free!"
The resulting roar of the legions shook the basin. Alexander permanently christened his imperial lineage House Vallius, fundamentally binding the identity of his people, his military, and his continent to the very earth they defended.
SECTION V: THE SEVEN-YEAR ELVEN WAR (127 AW – 133 AW)
Alarmed by the sudden emergence of a unified human superpower on their western borders, the aristocratic lords of the Fourth Elven Empire issued an imperial ultimatum: Alexander was to immediately dismantle his standing legions, dissolve his central council, and resume paying heavy ancestral tributes in gold and grain to the Elven capital. Alexander tore the document in half before the elven emissaries. The High Elves declared total war.
The conflict raged continuously for seven brutal years (127 AW – 133 AW). It was a catastrophic clash of fundamentally different military philosophies:
* The Elven War Machine: Relied on centuries of combat experience, flawless tactical discipline, devastating air-support lines, and high-attunement elemental mages capable of reshaping battlefields with a single evocation.
* The Vallian War Machine: Fueled by endless human adaptation, relentless logistical reinforcement managed by Constantine, and Alexander’s unyielding refusal to accept defeat. Alexander lost severe tactical engagements, suffered catastrophic troop depletions, and watched his senior officers take horrific wounds—but he meticulously studied every failure, adapted his formations, and never once ordered a retreat from a theater of war.
SECTION VI: THE GRACE OF THE IRON VALLEY (133 AW)
The Killing Field
In 133 AW, the climax of the war manifested within the treacherous confines of the Iron Valley—a jagged, claustrophobic mountain gorge streaked with dark veins of heavy raw iron. The veteran Elven General, an immortal commander hundreds of years old who had never lost a single military engagement, had baited the Vallians into a flawless tactical bottleneck.
[ ELVEN MAGES ON RIDGES ]                           [ ELVEN MAGES ON RIDGES ]
   ▼   ▼   ▼   ▼   ▼                                   ▼   ▼   ▼   ▼   ▼
=============================================================================
                  [ HIGH-RAIN OF ARROWS / ELEMENTAL FIRE ]
                                     |
                                     ▼
                     [ PINNED VALLIAN INFANTRY LINE ]
                                     ▲
                                     |
                         [ JULIUS'S ROYAL CHARGE ]
=============================================================================


The battlefield quickly turned into a slaughterhouse. Elven elemental mages completely lined the high, inaccessible ridges, raining down continuous sheets of arcane fire, while cloaked elven archers poured thousands of arrows into the pinned Vallian infantry below.
The Sacrifice of Julius
Realizing his army was on the verge of being systematically pulverized, Alexander drew his blade, preparing to personally lead a suicidal frontal assault up the cliffside. Julius, seeing the absolute ruin of the empire if the crown fell, physically grabbed Alexander’s arm, locking eyes with him with an unprecedented, grim gravity.
Julius wrenched his arm away, drew his sword, and roared a final command to the royal guard. He personally spearheaded the near-impossible charge up the steep rock face. Under an apocalyptic hail of arrows and kinetic spells, Julius fought with a terrifying, demonic ferocity. He reached the summit, breached the elven lines, and broke the concentration of the mages. The main Vallian force poured through the resulting gap, completely turning the tide of the battle.
The Death of Julius
During the frantic, bleeding chaos of the ridge breakthrough, the Elven General’s second-in-command—a highly favored, legendary lieutenant who had fought beside the general for centuries—spotted an opening. Slipped through a hidden, narrow goat path, he emerged directly into the blind spot of Alexander’s command position, raising his greatblade for a fatal execution strike.
Julius, bleeding from multiple arrow wounds, caught the movement from the corner of his eye. Without a single moment of hesitation, he threw his body directly into the path of the blade.
The elven steel completely pierced Julius's chest. Alexander spun, his vision blurring as he witnessed his most trusted friend collapse. Before the elven lieutenant could even retract his weapon for a second thrust, Alexander’s blade severed his head from his shoulders before the body could even hit the soil.
Alexander caught Julius as he fell, dropping to his knees on the blood-soaked grass. Tears cut tracks through the grime on both their faces.
"Tell my wife..." Julius whispered, coughing violently as the life faded from his eyes. "Tell her I fought bravely. Tell her... I am not a coward."
Alexander held him tighter, his voice breaking: "You were never a coward, Julius. Never."
A faint, characteristically sharp smile crossed Julius's lips. "No. I was. Just... not today."
Julius died within the Archon's arms. Alexander wept openly, experiencing a grief far deeper and more lacerating than the day his father was taken. He laid his companion down, stood up slowly, his hands dripping with royal blood, his eyes raw, crimson, and wet with tears.
The Duel of Cold Rage
The immortal Elven General descended the ridge alone to meet him. He was older, physically stronger, possessed vastly superior reach, and carried centuries of undefeated dueling experience. The entire continent held its breath as the two commanders closed the distance.
The Elven General initiated the assault with blinding, hyper-optimized speed, instantly driving Alexander back, cutting through his guard, and opening deep wounds across his arms and chest. By every metric of martial science, Alexander should have been carved to pieces within the minute.
But the tears never stopped streaming down Alexander’s face. This was not a manifestation of fear—it was an absolute, blinding torrent of cold, hyper-focused grief and apocalyptic rage. It was a spiritual manifestation so pure and absolute that even Malakor, the God of War, had never witnessed its like: a sorrow so devastating that it transformed into an invincible physical weapon.
Alexander stopped feeling the lacerations. He adapted to the general’s centuries-old patterns within seconds, matching his speed and breaking his pacing. With a final, explosive parry, Alexander shattered the Elven General's guard, disarmed him, and sent him crashing into the dirt, the point of the Vallian steel pressed firmly against the immortal's throat.
The Elven General closed his eyes, silently awaiting the inevitable execution.
Alexander stood over him, his chest heaving, his face wet with tears. Slowly, he lowered the blade.
"Get up," Alexander commanded coldly.
The general opened his eyes, completely uncomprehending. "Why do you stay your hand, human?"
"I have lost my father to cowardly assassins," Alexander whispered, his voice echoing across the silent valley. "I have lost my brother to a blade meant for my own throat. I will not forfeit my honor to this mud today. Get up. Return to your legions. Tell your high lords that Alexander of House Vallius does not slaughter a defeated foe."
Humbled and fundamentally changed by an act of chivalric mercy that broke every convention of elven superiority, the Elven General stood, offered a profound, deep martial bow, and marched back to his lines. Within the hour, the Fourth Elven Empire ordered a total surrender. The war was finished.
SECTION VII: THE EYE OF THE PANTHEON
High above the blood-soaked iron cliffs, the cosmic entities of the Pantheon looked down upon the theater of mortality, forever altered by what they had observed:
* Malakor (The Iron Wrath): Stared down in total, stunned silence. The God of War had never witnessed an organic rage that could conquer an undefeated army and then instantly transition into absolute, magnanimous mercy.
* Valerius (The Vanguard): Wept silent, silver tears, witnessing the absolute peak of mortal sacrifice, honor, and vanguard protection.
* Solari (The Sovereign Dawn): Nodded in grand imperial approval, recognizing the definitive rise of a rightful sovereign capable of bringing absolute order out of absolute chaos.
* Anima (The Primal Bloom): Smiled from the fringes, watching the human lineage sprout from fragile seedlings into a force that dominated the landscape.
* Discordia (The Unbound Chaos): Let loose a delighted, ringing laugh across the astral currents, declaring: "This one... this one is a beautiful paradox. I will be watching."*
SECTION VIII: THE PAX VALLIA AND THE ROYAL LINE (133 AW – 144 AW)
The Conquest of the Margins
Following the historic triumph at the Iron Valley, the Fourth Elven Empire formally abdicated their rule over the lowlands, retreating permanently into their highly insulated, fortified eastern mountain strongholds. They no longer held dominion over the continent.
Alexander spent the next two years (133 AW – 135 AW) completing his grand sweep of the territory. He marched his veteran legions to the western silver coast, secured the northern iron marches, mapped the high sunspire mountains, and established treaties within the deepwoods. Everywhere his banners flew, he extended the same immutable foundation: Surrender and receive full integration, absolute protection, and imperial citizenship; resist, and face absolute tactical deconstruction.
The Great Naming
In 135 AW, Alexander officially stripped the ancient elven name of Aurelia from the world archives. On every map, trade manifest, and diplomatic decree, the land was permanently rechristened Vallia. Within a single decade, an eighteen-year-old orphan had named his people, founded his empire, and named an entire continent after the valleys of his home.
                 [ ARCHON ALEXANDER THE GREAT ]
                     ( House Vallius - 135 AW )
                                 |
                     +-----------+-----------+
                     |                       |
           [ ELARA OF LYSANDRIA ]   [ IMPERIAL ADMINISTRATION ]
              ( Wed in 139 AW )        ( Infrastructure & Law )
                     |
         +-----------+-----------+
         |                       |
 [ NICOLAUS VALLIUS ]   [ ALEXANDER VALLIUS II ]
   ( Born 140 AW )         ( Born 141 AW )


Domestic Governance and Lineage
From 135 AW to 140 AW, Alexander proved himself an equally capable peace-time administrator. He engineered a continental network of stone highways, codified standardized imperial trade laws via Constantine, and organized a permanent standing military.
* The Marriage: In 139 AW, at the age of 34, Alexander married a noblewoman named Elara, a daughter of Lysandrian aristocracy.
* The Heirs: In 140 AW, Elara gave birth to their firstborn son, christened Nicolaus in honor of Alexander’s late father. In 141 AW, their second son was born, named Alexander II.
SECTION IX: THE GREAT DISAPPEARANCE (145 AW)
By 144 AW, the Emperor grew increasingly restless. He was only 39 years old, yet he had already accomplished every terrestrial milestone imaginable. He began spending late nights in the palace astronomical spires, staring out toward the eastern horizons beyond the mapped mountain holds of the Elves. He spoke openly to his war council of launching a massive grand expedition to map what lay beyond the literal edge of the known world.
In 145 AW, at the age of 40, Alexander the Great completely vanished.
* The Mystery: There was no struggle, no political coup, no trace of poison, and no assassination plot. One morning the Emperor was sitting at his administrative desk; by the following dawn, his personal chambers were entirely vacant.
* The Divine Silence: Not even the low-frequency scrying spells of the Qashari or the eyes of the Pantheon could detect his location or his soul's signature.
* The Myth: Local folklore quickly filled the void. Some whispered that the Great Aether itself reached down to pull its finest creation back into the cosmic field; others feared he accidentally touched a hidden patch of the Void beyond the mountains. The common citizens maintained that he merely walked out into the world as a wanderer, waiting for the day his people would need his blade once more.
SECTION X: THE TRIUMVIRATE REGENCY AND THE SECOND EMPEROR (145 AW – 160 AW)
The Fifteen-Year Interregnum
Because Alexander was taken at the absolute peak of his life, he had not yet drafted a formal succession law or officially appointed an imperial heir. To prevent the continent from fracturing back into independent city-states, his three surviving generals stepped into the vacuum:
* Honorius: Governed the standing military, ensuring total peace and security across the borders.
* Constantine: Managed the imperial treasury, maintaining absolute continuity of trade and resource flow.
* Augustus: Administered domestic policy and border defenses, holding the Elven mountain holds at bay.
For fifteen years (145 AW – 160 AW), the three generals ruled together as an unbroken, fiercely loyal Co-Regency, holding the massive fabric of Vallia together while Alexander's young sons came of age.
              [ THE TRIUMVIRATE REGENCY ] (145 AW - 160 AW)
       +----------------------------+----------------------------+
       |                            |                            |
  [ HONORIUS ]                [ CONSTANTINE ]               [ AUGUSTUS ]
(Military Control)          (Treasury & Finance)         (Domestic Defense)


The Ascension of Alexander II
In 160 AW, nearly fifteen years after the disappearance, the Triumvirate organized the first democratic Imperial Election across the continent to determine the rightful successor. Alexander II, possessing his father’s sharp features and commanding presence, won the vote by an overwhelming landslide. He ascended the throne as the second official Emperor of Vallia.
The Legacy of the Sarcophagus
Alexander the Great's physical body was never recovered. Beneath the foundations of the High Imperial Palace in the capital, an immense, empty sarcophagus carved from absolute white marble sits in perpetuity. It contains no human remains; it is a permanent cosmic anchor to a man who refused to be broken by defeat, who suffered directly alongside his men, and who built the very bedrock of human civilization on Terra.
The golden age of the Pax Vallia flourished under his descendants, but it was Alexander who carved the space out of the wilderness, leaving an empire that would endure for generations.
  


—-- 


Celeste “The Mother”
Era: The Imperial Period, approximately 3610 AW to 3640 AW
Location: The Palace of Aurelia, Vallia
Character: Empress Celeste of House Vallius, the first and only empress, called the Mother
________________


The Senate had not wanted her.
They had wanted almost anyone else. But Julius X of House Julius had died without an heir. A hunting accident, they said. An arrow gone wrong. Celeste never believed it. Julius had been a drunk and a fool, but he had been skilled with a bow. Someone had wanted him dead. Someone had wanted the throne empty.
The election was called. The five houses put forward their candidates.
House Aurelius put forward General Maximus, a war hero with a hundred victories and no political sense. The legions loved him. The Senate feared him. He was a hammer looking for a nail.
House Julius put forward Senator Decimus, a master of rhetoric and bribery. He had bought half the Senate already. He expected to buy the rest.
House Constantinus put forward Merchant Prince Lorenzo, the wealthiest man in Vallia. He had funded three emperors and bankrupted two. He believed gold could buy anything, including a throne.
House Augustus put forward Governor Valens, a popular leader from the provinces. He promised autonomy, lower taxes, and peace. The provinces loved him. The capital did not know him.
House Vallius put forward Celeste.
She was the granddaughter of Alexander XVI, a respected emperor who had ruled for thirty years. Her father had died in a border skirmish. Her mother had died of plague. Her brothers had been lost to war and disease. She was the last of her line.
The other houses laughed. A woman? A woman with no army, no gold, no political machine? They dismissed her.
She did not dismiss them.
She spent the next six months preparing. She did not campaign in the traditional sense. She did not give speeches. She did not distribute gold. She did not threaten. She listened.
She visited the legions. She did not promise them victory. She promised them care. She visited the wounded. She visited the widows. She learned the names of fallen soldiers. The legions did not forget.
She visited the merchants. She did not promise them lower taxes. She promised them stability. She showed them her plan for the roads, the ports, the aqueducts. The merchants did not forget.
She visited the provinces. She did not promise them autonomy. She promised them a voice. She listened to their grievances. She wrote them down. The provinces did not forget.
She visited the Senate. She did not promise them power. She promised them order. She told them that she would not be a puppet. She told them that she would not be a tyrant. She told them that she would be an emperor. The Senate did not believe her. But they did not forget.
The election came. The Senate voted.
General Maximus received thirty votes. Senator Decimus received forty. Merchant Prince Lorenzo received twenty. Governor Valens received twenty five.
Celeste received the rest.
One hundred and eighty five votes. A landslide.
The Senate was stunned. The houses were furious. The people cheered.
"How?" Decimus demanded. "How did you win?"
Celeste smiled. "I asked for what I wanted. You tried to buy what you wanted. There is a difference."
She was crowned on the first day of spring. She was twenty eight years old. She was the first and only empress of Vallia.
________________


The Mother
Her first years were difficult. The five houses tested her. House Aurelius demanded more funding for the legions. She gave them half and told them to prove they deserved the rest. House Constantinus demanded lower taxes on trade. She raised them instead and used the revenue to repair the aqueducts. House Julius tried to outmaneuver her in the Senate. She outmaneuvered them instead. House Augustus demanded more autonomy for the provinces. She granted it, then appointed her own governors to oversee them. House Vallius, her own house, expected her to be a figurehead. She reminded them that she was the emperor.
But it was not the Senate that gave her the name. It was the people.
The plague came in her second year.
It swept through the poor districts of Aurelia like a wildfire. The rich fled to their country estates. The doctors quarantined themselves in their clinics. The priests prayed behind closed doors. Celeste stayed.
She walked into the plague districts. She had no magic. She had no medicine. She had a cloth mask and a basket of bread. She visited the sick. She held the hands of the dying. She comforted children who had lost their parents.
"We cannot save everyone," she told her guards. "But we can let them know they are not alone."
A young mother, dying of fever, clutched Celeste's hand. "My daughter," she whispered. "She is only three. She has no one."
Celeste took the child. She raised her in the palace. The girl grew up to become a scholar, a healer, a woman who saved thousands of lives. Her name was Lucia. She never called Celeste Empress. She called her Mother.
The people saw. The people remembered.
They began to call her the Mother. Not as an insult. As an honor. She was the mother of the city. The mother of the poor. The mother of the forgotten.
The Senate tried to mock her. "The Mother," Decimus sneered. "As if the empire were a nursery."
But the name stuck. The people would not let it go.
________________


Her Sons
Celeste married late, at thirty five. Her husband was a scholar, a quiet man from House Aethel, the knowledge house. He had no interest in politics. He loved books and gardens. She loved him for that.
They had two sons. Robertus and Nicolaus.
Robertus was the elder. He was quiet, thoughtful, and responsible. He followed his father into scholarship. He loved books. He loved history. He loved order. He never gave his mother a moment of worry.
Nicolaus was the younger. He was none of those things.
He ran with latrones, gangs of thieves and brawlers in the back alleys of Aurelia. He wore rough clothes and spoke rough words. He came home with bruises and split lips. He laughed when his mother tried to scold him.
"You are a prince of Vallia," she said. "You could be anything. Why do you choose to be a latro?"
"I am not a latro," Nicolaus said. "I am a survivor. There is a difference."
He had friends in low places. Dock workers. Street vendors. Former gladiators. Freed slaves. They called him Nicolaus the Wolf. They did not care that his mother was the empress. They cared that he was loyal.
Celeste worried. She sent guards to watch him. He evaded them. She sent spies to follow him. He befriended them. She sent Vex, her shadow, to bring him home. Nicolaus talked to Vex for an hour. Vex returned alone.
"What did he say?" Celeste asked.
"He said that you are the mother of the empire, but you cannot be the mother of every lost boy in Aurelia. He said that someone has to watch the alleys. He said that someone has to protect the ones who fall through the cracks."
Celeste was silent for a long time. Then she smiled.
"He is more like me than I thought."
________________


The Reckoning
The turning point came when Nicolaus was twenty two.
A rival gang had hurt one of his men. Beat him nearly to death. Left him in an alley to bleed. Nicolaus wanted revenge. He gathered his crew. He sharpened his knife. He was going to kill.
His brother Robertus found him.
Robertus was not a fighter. He was a scholar. He had soft hands and a softer heart. He stood in front of Nicolaus and did not move.
"Get out of my way," Nicolaus said.
"No."
"I said get out of my way."
"You are not a killer, brother. You are a boy who got lost. Come home. Mother is waiting."
Nicolaus laughed. "Mother is always waiting. She has been waiting for twenty two years for me to become someone I am not."
"She has been waiting for you to become who you are. There is a difference."
Nicolaus lowered his knife.
He did not go to the fight. He went home. He walked into the palace, blood still on his hands, and found his mother in the garden. She was planting flowers. She did not look up.
"I am sorry," he said.
She looked up. Her eyes were wet.
"I know."
"I am not going to be a scholar like Robertus. I am not going to write books or teach students. I am not going to sit in a library and be quiet."
She nodded. "I know."
"But I am not going to be a latro anymore either. I am going to be something else. I just do not know what yet."
She stood. She walked to him. She put her hand on his cheek.
"You will find it. You are my son. You will find it."
________________


The Healer
Nicolaus found his purpose in the clinics.
He visited Lucia, the orphan his mother had saved from the plague. Lucia was a healer now. She ran a free clinic in the poorest district of Aurelia. She had no money, no supplies, no help.
Nicolaus offered his help.
"What do you know about healing?" Lucia asked.
"Nothing. But I know how to fight. I know how to protect. I can keep the gangs away from your door."
Lucia laughed. "The gangs are afraid of you?"
"They are afraid of my mother. That is enough."
Nicolaus became the guardian of the clinic. He kept the peace. He carried supplies. He learned to bandage wounds. He learned to comfort the dying. He learned to hold a child's hand.
He was not a scholar. He was not a warrior. He was a healer.
________________


His Own Family
When Nicolaus was thirty, he met a woman named Flavia. She was a nurse at the clinic, a quiet woman with strong hands and a gentle voice. She had been a slave, freed by one of Celeste's reforms. She owed the empress her life. She gave her loyalty freely.
Nicolaus and Flavia married in a small ceremony in the palace garden. Celeste wept with joy. Robertus gave a speech. The clinic patients threw flowers.
They had three children. Two boys and a girl.
The eldest was named Lucius, after Celeste's father. He became a soldier. He served in the legions for twenty years. He never rose above centurion. He did not want to. He was content to lead his men and protect his people.
The second was named Valeria, after Celeste's mother. She became a scholar like her uncle Robertus. She studied the stars. She discovered three new comets. The Qashari named an observatory after her.
The youngest was named Alexander, after the great founder of Vallia. He became a healer like his father. He took over the clinic when Nicolaus grew old. He ran it for forty years.
Celeste lived long enough to see all three of them born. She held each of them in her arms. She sang to them the same songs she had sung to their father.
"They are not princes," Nicolaus said.
"They are better than princes," Celeste replied. "They are free."
________________


The Legacy
Celeste ruled for thirty years.
She reformed the tax code. She repaired the roads. She built new aqueducts. She established schools for girls as well as boys. She invited Qashari scholars to teach at the University of Aurelia. She opened trade with the Jin. She made peace with the Skaldians. She paid the Oru to stop raiding. She sent emissaries to Sikuark. They never returned, but she kept sending them.
Robertus wrote his history. Nicolaus healed his patients. Celeste watched them both with pride.
She watched her grandchildren grow. Lucius the soldier. Valeria the scholar. Alexander the healer. She did not live to see them old. She saw them young. That was enough.
When she grew old, she called her sons to her bedside.
Robertus held her left hand. Nicolaus held her right.
"You are not emperors," she said. "You never will be. Are you content?"
Robertus spoke first. "I have written the history of our people. I have preserved the memory of our ancestors. I am content."
Nicolaus spoke second. "I have healed the sick. I have held the dying. I have raised children who will carry on my work. I am content."
Celeste smiled. "Then I have done my job."
She died that night. Peacefully. In her sleep.
The Senate voted. The empire did not fracture. The peace held.
Silas II of House Augustus became emperor. He honored Celeste's memory. He continued her policies.
Her statue was raised in the Great Forum of Aurelia, not far from the statue of Aurelian. It is smaller. She would have wanted it that way.
The inscription reads: She was the Mother of Vallia. Her sons did not rule. One wrote the past. One healed the present. Her grandchildren lived free. She left behind an empire.
Children still visit her statue. They leave flowers. They whisper prayers. They call her Mother.
Robertus wrote the history. Nicolaus healed the sick. Lucius guarded the borders. Valeria studied the stars. Alexander carried on the healing.
And Celeste, the Mother, watched over them all.
________________


THE END 


THE FALL AND RISE OF VALLIA 
Era: The End of the Imperial Period, approximately 3790 AW to 3880 AW
Characters: Emperor Valerius IV of House Vallius, Cassian the Restorer of House Julius, and Cassian II
________________


Part One: The Weight of Blood
Valerius IV was born in 3758 AW. He was a descendant of the Vallian house, a great grandson of Theodosius II, the last strong emperor before the decline. Theodosius had ruled from 3700 to 3730 AW, a thirty year reign of stability and competence.
After Theodosius, the throne had passed to other houses. Solarian VI of House Aurelius had been a warmonger who drained the treasury. Alexander XVII of House Augustus had been a weak administrator who let the provinces slip away.
Now, in 3790 AW, the Senate looked to House Vallius again. Valerius was thirty two years old. He had no army, no fortune, no political machine. What he had was a name and a reputation for honesty. The people remembered Theodosius. They hoped Valerius would be like him.
He was not.
________________


Part Two: The Election
The election of 3790 AW was contested by five candidates.
House Aurelius put forward General Octavian, a war hero loved by the legions and feared by the Senate. House Julius put forward Senator Marcellus, a master of rhetoric and compromise. House Constantinus put forward Merchant Prince Hadrian, the wealthiest man in Vallia. House Augustus put forward Governor Tiberius, a popular leader from the eastern provinces.
House Vallius put forward Valerius.
He campaigned not in the Senate house, but in the streets. He visited the poor districts. He listened to the widows. He ate in the taverns and drank with the dock workers. He did not promise miracles. He promised to try.
The election was close. Marcellus led after the first round. Octavian led after the second. Hadrian dropped out and threw his support to Valerius. Tiberius dropped out and threw his support to Valerius. Marcellus and Octavian split the remaining votes.
Valerius won by a margin of twelve votes.
The Senate was stunned. The people cheered. Valerius stood on the balcony of the palace, looking out at the crowd, and wondered if he was worthy of his ancestors.
He was not.
________________


Part Three: The Emperor Who Could Not Lead
Valerius was not a bad man. He was a weak one. There is a difference.
He loved poetry and music. He loved the quiet of the library and the warmth of the hearth. He loved his wife, Cornelia, a woman he had met at a literary salon, a woman who shared his love of words and his hatred of violence.
He did not love politics. He did not love war. He did not love the crushing weight of an empire that had been falling apart for generations.
The provinces were slipping away. The Skaldians raided the northern coast. The Oru pirates blocked the southern shipping lanes. The Jin stopped answering messages. The Qashari closed their borders. The Elves grew bolder, reclaiming lands that had been Vallian for centuries.
Valerius tried. He appointed honest governors. He cut taxes for the poor. He sponsored festivals to keep the people happy. He wrote letters to the provincial leaders, begging them to stay loyal.
They did not stay loyal. They could not. The empire was bankrupt. The legions were underpaid. The roads were crumbling. The aqueducts were failing. A kind letter could not fix what centuries of neglect had broken.
"The empire is dying," Cornelia told him one night.
"I know."
"Then do something."
"What would you have me do?"
"Fight. Lead. Be an emperor."
Valerius looked at his hands. They were soft. They had never held a sword.
"I do not know how."
Cornelia loved him. She loved his gentleness, his kindness, his poetry. But she also loved the empire. She had grown up in the shadow of its greatness. She had dreamed of standing beside a man who would restore its glory.
She had chosen the wrong man.
"I am sorry," she said.
She left him that night. Not for another man. For the empire. She traveled to the provinces, rallying governors, raising armies, trying to hold together what her husband could not.
She died in 3810 AW. Assassinated by agents of a corrupt senator who did not want her interfering. Valerius received the news in his study. He stared at the letter for an hour. Then he put his head in his hands and wept.
He did not leave his chambers for a month. When he emerged, he was thinner, greyer, and more lost than ever.
The empire crumbled around him.
________________


Part Four: The Fall
By 3820 AW, Vallia was a corpse that had not yet stopped twitching.
The provinces had declared independence. The legions had stopped answering orders. The Senate had stopped meeting. The five houses had retreated to their strongholds, waiting for the end.
Valerius IV sat on the throne in Aurelia, alone except for a few loyal servants. He did not eat. He did not sleep. He wrote poetry. All of it was about Cornelia.
"The empire is dead," he wrote. "And I killed it with my indecision."
He did not kill himself. He did not have the courage for that either. He simply waited.
The Senate came to him in the winter of 3820 AW. They did not bow. They did not kneel.
"Valerius, you are no longer emperor. The Senate has voted. You are removed."
He nodded. "I know."
"Sign the abdication."
He signed. He walked out of the palace. He did not look back.
He died three years later, in 3823 AW, in a small villa outside Aurelia, surrounded by his books and his poems. He was 65 years old. His last words were Cornelia.
The empire was gone.
________________


Part Five: The Dark Years
For thirty years, Vallia had no emperor. No king. No central government.
The provinces fought each other. Warlords carved out small kingdoms. Bandits roamed the roads. The legions dissolved into mercenary companies. The five houses retreated to their ancestral lands and waited.
Aurelia became a ghost city. The population dropped from two million to less than two hundred thousand. The aqueducts broke. The streets filled with rubble. The great Forum of Aurelia, where Celeste's statue stood, became a cattle market.
The people called this period the Dark Years. They did not know it would end.
Cassian of House Julius was born in 3800 AW, twenty years before the fall. He was twenty years old when Valerius was removed. He witnessed the collapse as a young man. He saw the legions disband. He saw the provinces secede. He saw his father, a minor noble, lose everything.
He did not forget.
________________


Part Six: The Rise
Cassian was thirty years old when he decided to restore Vallia.
He had no army. He had no money. He had no allies. He had a name, a reputation, and a dream.
He started small. He traveled to the nearby villages, offering to settle disputes, to protect farmers from bandits, to rebuild bridges and clear roads. He did not ask for payment. He asked for loyalty.
Within five years, he controlled a region the size of a small province. Within ten years, he controlled the southern plains. Within fifteen years, he controlled half of what had once been Vallia.
He did not conquer. He united. He did not destroy. He rebuilt. He did not punish. He forgave.
The other houses watched. Some laughed. Some feared. Some waited.
House Aurelius was the first to join him. The military house had been waiting for a leader worth following. Cassian was not a great warrior. He was not a brilliant strategist. He was a man of character. That was enough.
House Augustus joined next. The provincial house had been waiting for a leader who would respect their autonomy. Cassian promised them a voice. He kept his promise.
House Constantinus joined reluctantly. The merchant house wanted stability. Cassian offered it. They paid for his roads. He protected their trade.
House Vallius was the last. The royal house had been leaderless for decades, drifting, purposeless. They had no candidate to put forward. They had no influence. They had no hope.
Cassian did not claim the throne. He did not want it. He wanted something new. But he also knew that he could not simply take power. He had to be chosen.
________________


Part Seven: The Election of 3850 AW
In 3850 AW, thirty years after the fall, the five houses finally agreed to hold an election. The Senate was reconvened. The provinces sent representatives. The people gathered in the streets of Aurelia, which was still scarred but slowly healing.
Five candidates put forward their names.
House Aurelius put forward General Valens, a young commander who had distinguished himself in the border wars. House Constantinus put forward Merchant Prince Cassius, a wealthy banker who had funded much of the rebuilding. House Augustus put forward Governor Septimus, a popular leader from the eastern provinces. House Vallius put forward no one. They had no candidate worthy of the name.
House Julius put forward Cassian.
He was fifty years old. His hair was grey. His hands were calloused from years of labor. He was not a great speaker. He was not a wealthy man. He was not a famous general.
He was trusted.
The campaign was short. Cassian did not make promises. He did not give speeches. He visited the villages he had rebuilt. He walked the roads he had repaired. He stood in the forums of the towns he had saved.
"You know me," he said. "You have seen my work. You have eaten bread from my fields. You have drunk water from my aqueducts. If you want more of the same, vote for me. If you want something else, vote for someone else."
The people voted.
General Valens received seventy votes. Merchant Prince Cassius received sixty. Governor Septimus received fifty five. Cassian received the rest.
Two hundred and fifteen votes. A landslide.
The Senate was not stunned. They had expected it. The people had chosen.
Cassian was crowned not as emperor, but as king. He did not claim the title of emperor because the empire was dead. He was the first king of the Kingdom of Vallia.
The historians would later call him the 125th leader of Vallia. The people did not count. They called him the Restorer.
________________


Part Eight: The Acts of the Restorer
His first act was to confirm the new Senate. Not the corrupt Senate of the old empire. A new Senate, chosen by the provinces, chosen by the people. He gave them power. He did not keep it for himself.
His second act was to sign a charter of rights. It guaranteed the freedom of speech, the right to a fair trial, and the protection of property. It was not perfect. It did not end slavery or grant citizenship to all. But it was a beginning.
His third act was to visit the statue of Celeste in the Great Forum. The forum was still a cattle market. The statue was covered in mud and bird droppings.
Cassian knelt before it. He did not command anyone to clean it. He cleaned it himself. He scrubbed the mud from Celeste's face. He wiped the droppings from her robes.
The people watched. They did not know what to make of him.
"Why are you doing that?" a woman asked.
"Because she was the Mother of Vallia," Cassian said. "And because someone should remember."
The woman picked up a rag. She knelt beside him. She scrubbed.
By the end of the day, the statue was clean. The cattle were gone. The people stayed.
________________


Part Nine: The Love
Cassian married late. He was fifty five years old. His wife was a woman named Valeria. She was not a noble. She was a farmer's daughter, a widow, a mother of two. She had lost her husband to bandits. She had lost her farm to drought. She had lost her hope to the Dark Years.
Cassian met her on a road in the southern plains. Her cart had broken a wheel. He stopped to help. He fixed the wheel. She offered him bread and cheese. He accepted.
They talked for an hour. Then two. Then three. The sun set. The stars came out.
"I have to go," he said.
"I know."
"I will come back."
"No, you will not. Kings do not come back for farmers' widows."
"You are not a farmer's widow. You are Valeria. And I will come back."
He came back. He came back every week for a year. He brought her flowers. He brought her books. He brought her seeds for her garden. He brought her hope.
They married in the small chapel where her first husband had been buried. The chapel had no roof. The stars were out. Cassian did not mind.
"I am not a queen," she said.
"You are my queen."
"I do not know how to be a queen."
"Neither do I know how to be a king. We will learn together."
They had one child, a son named Cassian, after his father.
________________


Part Ten: The Election of Cassian II
Cassian ruled for thirty years. He died in 3880 AW, at the age of 80. His son, Cassian II, was not his heir. There were no heirs in Vallia. The throne was not inherited. It was earned.
But Cassian II was a good man. He had learned from his father. He had worked alongside him. He had rebuilt villages, repaired roads, and planted fields. He knew the people. The people knew him.
The election of 3880 AW was contested by four candidates.
House Aurelius put forward a general. House Constantinus put forward a merchant. House Augustus put forward a governor. House Julius put forward Cassian II.
House Vallius put forward no one. They still had no candidate worthy of the name.
The campaign was short. Cassian II did not ride on his father's name. He walked the same roads his father had walked. He visited the same villages. He stood in the same forums.
"You know me," he said. "You know my father. You know my work. If you want it to continue, vote for me. If you want something else, vote for someone else."
The people voted.
Cassian II won. Not by a landslide. By a margin of twenty votes. It was enough.
He was crowned the second king of the Kingdom of Vallia. The historians called him the 126th leader of Vallia. The people called him Cassian the Younger. He was not a restorer. He was a keeper. He held what his father had built. He kept the peace. He kept the roads. He kept the schools.
He was not a legend. He did not need to be.
________________


Part Eleven: The Legacy
The election system never changed. Even to the present day, the kings of Vallia are chosen by the Senate and the five houses. Blood does not guarantee the throne. It never did. It never will.
The people remember Valerius IV as the emperor who could not lead. They remember Cassian the Restorer as the man who rebuilt. They remember Cassian II as the man who held.
They do not number them. They do not rank them. They remember.
In the Great Foundation, the afterlife realm of endurance and legacy, Valerius and Cassian walk different paths. They do not speak. They have nothing to say to each other.
But sometimes, in the iron mountains or the stone fortresses, their paths cross. Valerius looks away. Cassian nods. That is enough.
The empire is gone. The kingdom remains. The elections continue.
________________
