THE LAST LIGHT 
A Hero of the Elven Warring Kingdoms
Era: The First Kingdom Era, approximately 19,000 BA
Name: Aelar of House Solarius, called the Last Light, the Savior of Aurelia, the Shadow's Bane
Ancestor: Aurelian, the first demigod, the first emperor
________________


Part One: The Birth
Aelar was born in the darkness of the warring kingdoms. His mother died in childbirth. His father died in battle before he could walk. He was raised by the elders of House Solarius, the last remnants of the royal line, the fading memory of Aurelian's glory.
The elders told him stories of the First Empire. They told him of Aurelian, the first demigod, the first emperor, the greatest elf who ever lived. They told him how Aurelian united the tribes, built Aurelia, conquered the world. They told him how Aurelian died in peace, surrounded by family, honored by the gods.
"You are his descendant," the elders said. "His blood flows in your veins. Not his power. His blood. His legacy. His duty."
Aelar did not feel powerful. He felt small. He felt scared. He felt like a boy who had lost everything.
But he listened. He learned. He trained.
By the time he was fifty, he was the finest swordsman in House Solarius. By the time he was a hundred, he was the finest general. By the time he was two hundred, he was the last hope of the Elves.
________________


Part Two: The Burden
The war had been raging for centuries. The Shadow King's army had conquered kingdom after kingdom. The rivers ran red. The skies were choked with smoke. The ground was thick with ashes.
House Solarius had retreated to Aurelia. The last city. The last light.
The elders looked to Aelar.
"You must lead us," they said. "You are the descendant of Aurelian. You are the last light."
Aelar did not want to lead. He did not want to be the last light. He wanted to be a soldier. He wanted to fight. He wanted to die with his comrades.
But he was the descendant of Aurelian. He had a duty.
"I will lead," he said. "But I will not lead from the back. I will stand with my soldiers. I will bleed with my soldiers. I will die with my soldiers."
The elders nodded. They had expected nothing less.
________________


Part Three: The Siege
The Shadow King's army surrounded Aurelia. The siege lasted for a year.
Aelar walked the walls every night. He spoke to the soldiers. He learned their names. He remembered their faces.
"Do not lose hope," he said. "Aurelia has stood for thousands of years. It will not fall tonight. It will not fall tomorrow. It will not fall while we still draw breath."
The soldiers believed him. Not because he was a great speaker. Because he was there. Because he bled with them. Because he fought beside them.
He took wounds on the walls. An arrow in the shoulder. A stone to the ribs. A sword cut across his face. He did not retreat. He did not hide. He stood.
The soldiers saw him. They fought harder.
________________


Part Four: The Final Battle
After a year of siege, the Shadow King gathered his army for one final assault. He would not starve the city. He would burn it.
Aelar watched from the walls. The Shadow King's army stretched across the plain, thousands strong, black against the red sky.
"There are too many," a soldier whispered.
"There are never too many," Aelar said. "There are only the ones who stand and the ones who fall."
He opened the gates.
His army marched out. They were outnumbered ten to one.
The battle was brutal. It was bloody. It was the worst slaughter since the Fall.
Aelar fought in the center of the field. His sword was a blur. His shield was cracked. His armor was drenched in blood. His blood. Enemy blood. It did not matter.
He saw the Shadow King across the field. Vaelen was cutting down elves with his black blade. He was laughing.
"Burn it!" he screamed. "Burn it all!"
Aelar pushed through the chaos. He fought his way toward the monster.
________________


Part Five: The Duel
They met at the base of the walls of Aurelia, where the stones were wet with blood and the air was thick with smoke.
"Vaelen," Aelar said.
"Aelar," Vaelen said. "The last of the Solarius. The last light of the Elves. How fitting that I should kill you here, at the feet of your ancestors."
"You will not kill me."
"I have killed everyone else. Why would you be different?"
They fought.
Vaelen was stronger. He was faster. He had been killing for three hundred years. Aelar was young. He was tired. He was wounded.
But he was fighting for Aurelia. He was fighting for the memory of Aurelian. He was fighting for hope.
He took a wound to his arm. A wound to his leg. A wound to his side. He kept fighting.
He took a wound to his shoulder. A wound to his ribs. A wound to his face. He kept fighting.
Vaelen grew frustrated. "Why will you not die?"
"I have not been given permission," Aelar said.
He saw an opening. Vaelen's guard dropped for a fraction of a second. Aelar struck.
His blade pierced Vaelen's chest.
Vaelen fell to his knees. Blood poured from his wound. He looked up at Aelar. He looked at the walls of Aurelia behind him. The white stone was stained with smoke and blood. The golden light was fading.
"You should not have come back," Aelar said. "You should have stayed in the shadows."
"I am a child of the shadows," Vaelen whispered. "I was born there. I should have died there."
Aelar raised his sword. His voice was cold.
"No," he said. "You will not die there. You will die here. At the gates of Aurelia. At the feet of the city you tried to burn."
He drove the blade through Vaelen's heart.
Vaelen gasped. He clutched at the sword. He looked up at Aelar one last time.
"History will remember me," he said.
"Yes."
"They will call me a monster."
"Yes."
"They will fear my name forever."
"Yes."
Vaelen smiled. Blood ran from his lips.
"Good."
He fell forward. He died in the dirt at the gates of Aurelia.
________________


Part Six: The Victory
Aelar stood over the body. He did not weep. He did not smile. He turned and walked back to the city.
"Burn the body," he said. "Scatter the ashes. But do not forget his name. Let him be a warning. Let him be a stain."
The soldiers cheered. The siege was over. Aurelia was saved.
Aelar did not cheer. He walked to the walls. He looked out at the battlefield. The dead were scattered across the plain like fallen leaves. His friends. His comrades. His soldiers.
He wept.
Not for the victory. For the cost. 
—
THE SECOND ELVEN EMPIRE 
The Military Government
Era: The First Kingdom Era, approximately 15,500 BA to 7,500 BA (8,000 years)
________________


Part One: The Founding
Valandor, head of House Valoris, declared himself Emperor of the Second Elven Empire. He was old. He was scarred. He had lost an eye and a hand in the wars. But he was respected. He was feared. He was strong.
He ruled with an iron fist. He abolished the councils. He disbanded the local militias. He imposed martial law on the provinces.
The other houses watched in silence. They did not like Valandor. They did not trust him. But they could not oppose him.
Valandor ruled for two hundred years. He died in battle, leading his legions against a rebellion in the north. His successor was chosen by the generals, not by blood.
The Valoris dynasty had begun. But it was not a dynasty of inheritance. It was a dynasty of strength. Only the strong ruled. The weak were deposed. The foolish were killed. The lucky survived.
________________


Part Two: The Last Emperor
After eight thousand years, the Valoris dynasty had grown tired. The emperors were no longer the strongest. They were the most paranoid. They saw enemies everywhere. They executed their own generals. They imprisoned their own advisors. They taxed the provinces into poverty.
The last emperor was named Maegor. He was not strong. He was cruel. He was paranoid. He had executed three of his best generals on suspicion of treason. He had imprisoned the heads of four houses.
The other houses watched. They had been waiting for centuries. They had been rebuilding their armies in secret. They had been planning.
"The Valoris have lost their way," said the head of House Solarius. "They are no longer protectors. They are tyrants."
The rebellion began in the forests. House Sylvana attacked a legion garrison. They burned the fortress. They freed the prisoners.
The rebellion spread to the coasts. House Pelagor sank the imperial fleet. They blockaded the ports.
The rebellion reached the heartland. House Solarius marched on Aurelia. The legions were divided. Some stayed loyal. Some joined the rebels.
The civil war lasted for a hundred years. The Valoris dynasty was defeated. Their legions were scattered. Their generals were executed. Their name became a curse.
The last emperor, Maegor, was captured in his palace. He was dragged through the streets of Aurelia. The people threw stones. They spat on him.
He was executed at the gates of the city, the same gates where Vaelen had died.
The Second Elven Empire fell.
KORR STONEHAND
A Dwarven Hero of the Second Elven Empire
Era: The Military Era (Second Elven Empire), approximately 12,000 BA
Clan: Ferrum-Smith
Title: The Stonehand, the Gate Breaker, the Unyielding
________________


Part One: The Mountain
Korr was born in Karaz Stein, the oldest dwarven hold, deep in the Central Mountains of what would one day be Vallia. His father was a miner. His mother was a smith. He was neither. He was a warrior.
He was not the strongest. He was not the fastest. He was the most stubborn.
The dwarves of the Second Elven Empire lived under the shadow of elven domination. The Elves did not rule the dwarves. They could not. The mountains were too deep, the tunnels too narrow, the holds too well defended. But the Elves controlled the passes. They controlled the trade routes. They controlled the surface.
Korr hated them.
Not because they were elves. Because they were arrogant. Because they looked down on the dwarves. Because they thought the mountains belonged to them.
"The mountains belong to the dwarves," Korr said. "They always have. They always will."
________________


Part Two: The Gate
The Elves built a fortress at the southern pass of the Central Mountains. They called it Ironwatch. It was a wall of stone and magic, designed to control the flow of goods between the dwarven holds and the elven heartland.
The dwarves paid tribute. They had no choice.
Korr chose differently.
He gathered a small band of warriors. Not an army. A strike force. He did not ask for permission. He did not wait for orders. He acted.
They tunneled under the mountain for three months. Not around the fortress. Under it.
On the night of the winter solstice, Korr and his warriors emerged inside Ironwatch. They killed the guards. They opened the gates. They burned the fortress.
The elves sent legions to reclaim the pass. Korr held it. He did not have an army. He had a hammer and a wall of stone.
"The pass is ours," he said. "If you want it, come and take it."
The elves came. They died. They came again. They died again.
After three years, the elves gave up. The pass remained in dwarven hands.
________________


Part Three: The Stonehand
Korr lost his hand in the fighting. An elven sword, enchanted with cold magic, froze his fingers solid. He shattered them on a rock and kept fighting.
He forged a new hand from iron. Not a prosthetic. A weapon. He named it the Stonehand.
"Elves took my hand," he said. "I made a better one."
The dwarves called him Korr Stonehand after that. The elves called him the Gate Breaker. He did not care what they called him.
________________


Part Four: The Legacy
Korr did not become king. He did not want to. He returned to Karaz Stein. He worked in the forges. He trained young warriors. He told stories of the siege of Ironwatch.
"The elves thought they could control us," he said. "They were wrong. The mountains do not bow. Neither do the dwarves."
He died old, in his bed, surrounded by his children and grandchildren. His iron hand was placed on his chest. His hammer was buried with him.
The dwarves built a statue of him at the southern pass. Not at the fortress. The fortress was gone. The pass was free.
The statue shows Korr standing on a pile of broken elven shields, his iron hand raised, his hammer in his other hand. His face is stern. His eyes are cold.
The inscription reads: "He broke the gate. He held the pass. He never bowed."
________________


Part Five: The Afterlife
Korr went to the Great Foundation. Not the Aurealis. He was not honored enough. Not the Twilight Labyrinth. He was not shadowy enough. Not Hell. He was not evil.
The Great Foundation. Where the builders go. Where the defenders go. Where the stubborn go.
Aethelgard welcomed him. The god of architecture and endurance looked at Korr's iron hand.
"You held the pass," Aethelgard said.
"For three years."
"Alone?"
"With my people."
Aethelgard nodded. "That is endurance."
Korr dwells in the iron mountains of the Great Foundation. He does not fight. He builds. He forges. He waits.
The dwarves still sing of him. They sing of the Gate Breaker. The Stonehand. The Unyielding.
They sing of a dwarf who refused to bow.
________________


THE LAY OF KORR STONEHAND
A song sung by dwarven miners in the deep halls
The elves built a gate of stone,
To keep the dwarves alone.
They thought the pass was theirs to hold,
They thought the dwarves would do as told.
But Korr was born of mountain deep,
An oath he swore, a vow to keep.
"The pass is ours," he said to them,
"The mountains do not bow."
He tunneled through the mountain's heart,
Three months of stone and dust and dark.
He burst the gate on winter's night,
And put the elven guards to flight.
The legions came. The legions died.
The pass ran red. The dwarves held wide.
For three long years, the hammer sang,
And Ironwatch to ruin sprang.
Korr lost his hand to elven steel,
He forged a new one, hard as keel.
"Elves took my hand," he said with glee,
"I made a better one, you see."
The dwarves still sing of Korr the Bold,
The Stonehand, and the tale is told:
The pass is free. The gate is down.
The dwarves will never bow.
—
THE SHATTERED CROWN
A Villain of the Elven Warring Kingdoms
Era: The First Kingdom Era, approximately 19,000 BA
Name: Vaelen of House Umbra, called the Shadow King, the Usurper, the Father of Ashes, the Stain on the Noctari
________________


Part One: The Fracture
The First Elven Empire had fallen. The Void Scar had been sealed. The Noctari had been exiled. The gods had returned to their realms, weary but watchful.
For a thousand years, the Elves had fought each other. House against house. Kingdom against kingdom. Brother against brother. The great cities of the First Empire lay in ruins. The roads were overgrown. The libraries were burned. The legions were scattered.
The gods watched. They did not interfere. The Elves had to find their own way.
In the chaos, a new kind of leader emerged. Not a unifier. A monster.
Vaelen of House Umbra was born into the shadows. His house had been cursed, exiled, driven into the Underdark. The Umbra were the architects of the Void ritual, the ones who had opened the rift, the ones who had shattered the empire. Their name was spoken with hatred across the elven lands.
Vaelen did not embrace the hatred. He fed on it. He grew strong on it. He became it.
He was young when he declared himself king of the Umbra. Not the Shadow Council. Not the elders. Himself. He killed his rivals in their sleep. He burned his father's hall. He took the throne of his house with blood and fire.
"House Umbra is not cursed," he said. "We are blessed. We opened the rift because we were strong enough to try. The others were too weak. They blamed us for their weakness. They exiled us for their fear."
His followers believed him. They were outcasts, exiles, the forgotten. They had nothing to lose. They gave him everything.
________________


Part Two: The Rise
Vaelen did not conquer quickly. He conquered cruelly.
He spent a century building his army. Not of soldiers. Of butchers. He recruited the worst of the exiles. Murderers. Torturers. Cannibals. He promised them blood. He promised them revenge. He promised them the world.
He attacked the weakest kingdom first. A small house on the edge of the continent. He did not slaughter the soldiers. He slaughtered everyone. Men, women, children. He burned the fields. He salted the earth. He left nothing.
He attacked the next kingdom. And the next. And the next.
He did not offer surrender. He did not take prisoners. He killed everyone who opposed him. He killed everyone who might oppose him. He killed everyone.
Within three hundred years, he controlled all but one of the elven lands. The rivers ran red. The skies were choked with smoke. The ground was thick with ashes.
Only Aurelia remained.
The capital. The jewel of the First Empire. The city built by Aurelian himself. The city of white stone and golden light.
Vaelen marched on Aurelia.
________________


Part Three: The Siege
The city had prepared. The walls were manned. The gates were barred. The last loyal army of the Elves stood ready to die.
House Solarius led them. The royal house. The descendants of Aurelian. They were few. Their general was young. Their cause seemed hopeless.
But they had something Vaelen did not. They had the memory of Aurelian. They had the legacy of the First Empire. They had hope.
The siege lasted for a year.
Vaelen's army surrounded the city. They built towers. They raised rams. They threw fire. They threw corpses. They threw themselves against the walls again and again.
The defenders held.
The young general, whose name was Aelar, walked the walls every night. He spoke to the soldiers. He learned their names. He remembered their faces.
"I will not let him take this city," he said. "This is Aurelia. This is the city of Aurelian. This is the last light of the Elves. If it falls, we fall. If it burns, we burn."
The soldiers cheered. They were tired. They were hungry. They did not break.
________________


Part Four: The Final Battle
After a year of siege, Vaelen grew impatient. He gathered his army for one final assault. He would not starve the city. He would burn it.
He marched his butchers to the gates of Aurelia. The sun was setting behind him. His army stretched across the plain, thousands strong, black against the red sky.
The defenders watched from the walls.
"There are too many," a soldier whispered.
"There are never too many," Aelar said. "There are only the ones who stand and the ones who fall."
He opened the gates.
His army marched out. They were outnumbered ten to one.
The battle was brutal. It was bloody. It was the worst slaughter since the Fall.
Vaelen fought in the center of the field, cutting down elves with his black blade. He was laughing.
"Burn it!" he screamed. "Burn it all!"
Aelar saw him. He pushed through the chaos. He fought his way toward the Shadow King.
They met at the base of the walls of Aurelia, where the stones were wet with blood and the air was thick with smoke.
"Vaelen," Aelar said.
"Aelar," Vaelen said. "The last of the Solarius. The last light of the Elves. How fitting that I should kill you here, at the feet of your ancestors."
"You will not kill me."
"I have killed everyone else. Why would you be different?"
They fought.
Vaelen was stronger. He was faster. He had been killing for three hundred years. Aelar was young. He was tired. He was wounded.
But he was fighting for Aurelia.
He was fighting for the memory of Aurelian.
He was fighting for hope.
He took a wound to his arm. A wound to his leg. A wound to his side. He kept fighting.
He took a wound to his shoulder. A wound to his ribs. A wound to his face. He kept fighting.
Vaelen grew frustrated. "Why will you not die?"
"I have not been given permission," Aelar said.
He saw an opening. Vaelen's guard dropped for a fraction of a second. Aelar struck.
His blade pierced Vaelen's chest.
________________


Part Five: The Death
Vaelen fell to his knees. Blood poured from his wound. He looked up at Aelar. He looked at the walls of Aurelia behind him. The white stone was stained with smoke and blood. The golden light was fading.
"You should not have come back," Aelar said. "You should have stayed in the shadows."
"I am a child of the shadows," Vaelen whispered. "I was born there. I should have died there."
Aelar raised his sword. His voice was cold.
"No," he said. "You will not die there. You will die here. At the gates of Aurelia. At the feet of the city you tried to burn."
He drove the blade through Vaelen's heart.
Vaelen gasped. He clutched at the sword. He looked up at Aelar one last time.
"History will remember me," he said.
"Yes."
"They will call me a monster."
"Yes."
"They will fear my name forever."
"Yes."
Vaelen smiled. Blood ran from his lips.
"Good."
He fell forward. He died in the dirt at the gates of Aurelia, his blood soaking into the stones that Aurelian had laid.
Aelar stood over him. He did not weep. He did not smile. He turned and walked back to the city.
"Burn the body," he said. "Scatter the ashes. But do not forget his name. Let him be a warning. Let him be a stain."
________________


Part Six: The Stain
Vaelen's body was burned outside the gates of Aurelia. His ashes were scattered in the wind. But his name was not erased. It was carved into the history of the Elves as a warning.
The Noctari inherited his legacy. They were already cursed by Valerius. Now they were stained by Vaelen. The other races looked at them and remembered the Shadow King. They remembered the rivers of blood. They remembered the fields of ash. They remembered the yearlong siege of Aurelia.
"The Noctari are like him," the Elves said. "They are all monsters."
It was not true. Most Noctari were not monsters. They were cursed, yes. Vulnerable to temptation, yes. But not monsters. Vaelen was a monster. Vaelen was the worst of them.
The stain never washed away.
________________


Part Seven: Hell
Vaelen's soul went to Vandor's gate. Vandor looked at him.
"You laid siege to Aurelia. You killed children. You burned fields. You salted the earth. You did not take prisoners. You did not offer mercy. You enjoyed it."
Vaelen said nothing.
"You are not going to Malakor's realm. You are not a warrior. You are a butcher."
Vaelen still said nothing.
"You are not going to Abyssa's Deep. You are not mad. You are cruel. There is a difference."
Vaelen waited.
"You are going to Hecate's Mire."
Vaelen's eyes widened.
"Where I will rot."
"Yes."
Vaelen was sent to Hell. Not to the battlegrounds. Not to the deep. To the mire.
Hecate's realm is a place of stagnant, toxic swamps, fields of decomposing matter, rivers of slow moving sludge. The air smells of rot and sulfur. Mushrooms the size of trees glow with sickly light.
Vaelen arrived naked, unarmed, alone.
He began to rot.
Not his body. His soul. Hecate's magic stripped away his memories, his ambitions, his cruelties. He felt them dissolve. He felt himself dissolve.
He tried to hold on. He could not.
He screamed. No one heard.
The Rotweavers came. They were not Akuma. They were not torturers. They were alchemists. They worked on Vaelen for centuries, breaking him down, transforming him into something new.
He is not dead. He is not alive. He is rotting.
He remembers nothing. Not his name. Not his deeds. Not his victories. He is a lump of decaying matter in a swamp, tended by creatures who do not speak, who do not care, who simply work.
Hecate visits him sometimes. She is curious.
"You wanted to burn Aurelia," she says. "Now you are less than ash. It is fitting."
Vaelen does not respond. He cannot.
________________


Part Eight: The Legacy
The Elves remember Vaelen. They remember the Shadow King. They remember the Father of Ashes. They remember the yearlong siege of Aurelia. They tell his story to their children.
"Be careful of the Noctari," they say. "They are cursed. They are vulnerable. They can become like him."
The Noctari remember him too. They hate him. He made their exile harder. He made their curse heavier. He gave the surface elves a reason to fear them, to despise them, to never trust them.
"He was one of us," the Noctari elders say. "But he was not like us. He was the worst of us. Do not become him."
The stain remains. It will never wash away.
And the gates of Aurelia still bear the scars of his siege. The stones were replaced, but the memory was not. Every elf who walks through those gates remembers the day the Shadow King came.
They remember. They fear. They do not forget.
